Threefold Division of Genus: Near, Distant, and Middle
Commentator explains the threefold division of genus into near, distant, and middle with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the near, distant, and middle genus for a given species and explain why the classification is relative.

Core Idea
Genus classification is relative—what is middle for one species may be near for another.

This passage introduces a threefold division of genus—near, distant, and middle—that goes beyond the standard twofold division. The commentator clarifies that 'middle' is a relative category: it refers to a genus that sits between the near and distant genera for a given species. Understanding this relativity is crucial when analyzing definitions in Islamic sciences, where terms like 'animal' or 'growing' may shift positions depending on the species being defined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the species under consideration
The commentator uses 'human' (الإنسان) as the primary example. Note which species is being analyzed; the genus classification changes with the species.
2
Find the distant genus (جنس بعيد)
The distant genus has no complete commonality above it. For human, it is 'substance' (الجوهر), the highest genus in that line.
In this text, 'distant' means the highest genus, not just any genus above the near.
3
Find the near genus (جنس قريب)
The near genus has no complete commonality beneath it—it is the immediate genus above the species. For human, it is 'animal' (الحيوان).
This matches the standard definition of near genus.
4
Identify the middle genus (جنس وسط)
The middle genus has both a genus above it and a genus below it. For human, the commentator gives 'growing' (النامي) as middle, since it has 'body' and 'substance' above and 'animal' below.
The middle genus is a subset of the distant genus—it lies between near and distant.
5
Check relativity of the middle genus
The commentator notes that 'growing' is middle for human but near for plants. This shows that genus classification depends on the species; what is middle for one can be near for another.
This relativity is a key insight beyond the standard twofold division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حَيْثُ قَالَ : ( جِنْسٌ قَرِيبٌ، أَوْ بَعِيدٌ، أَوْ وَسَط»، وَلَعَلَّ مُرَادَهُ بـ «الوَسَطِ» : بَعْضُ مَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهِ البَعِيدُ فِي القِسْمَةِ المَذْكُورَةِ، وَذَلِكَ بِأَنْ يُحْمَلَ : - البَعِيدُ عَلَى : مَا لَيْسَ فَوْقَهُ تَمَامُ مُشْتَرَك؛ كَـ : «الجَوْهَرِ» لـ «الإِنْسَانِ». - وَالقَرِيبُ عَلَى : مَا لَيْسَ تَحْتَهُ تَمَامُ مُشْتَرَك؛ كَ: «الحَيَوَانِ لَهُ. - وَالوَسَطُ عَلَى : مَا فَوْقَهُ تَمَامُ مُشْتَرَكَ وَتَحْتَهُ تَمَامُ مُشْتَرَك : «النَّامِي لَهُ، فَإِنَّ تَحْتَهُ كَـ الحَيَوَانُ وَفَوْقَهُ الجِسْمُ وَالجَوْهَرُ . وَهَذَا خِلَافُ المَعْرُوفِ، عَلَى أَنَّ مَا جَعَلَهُ وَسَطاً إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلإِنْسَانِ وَالفَرَسِ وَنَحْوِهِمَا ، وَهُوَ قَرِيبٌ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلنَّبَاتِ مَثَلاً كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ .
When he said: 'A genus, near or distant or middle', perhaps his intent by 'middle' is some of what the distant applies to in the mentioned division, and that is by applying: the distant to what does not have above it a complete commonality, like 'substance' for 'human'; and the near to what does not have beneath it a complete commonality, like 'animal' for it; and the middle to what has above it a complete commonality and beneath it a complete commonality: 'growing' for it, for beneath it is like 'animal' and above it 'body' and 'substance'. And this is contrary to the well-known, except that what he made middle is only relative to human and horse and the like, while it is near relative to plants, for example, as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the author's classification of genus into three types: near, distant, and middle. The commentator interprets 'middle' as something that falls under the distant genus but is not the farthest. He gives examples: for 'human', the distant genus is 'substance', the near genus is 'animal', and the middle genus is 'growing' (which is between body and animal). He notes that this classification contradicts the standard twofold division (near and distant) but argues that it is relative: 'growing' is middle for human but near for plants. The passage emphasizes the relativity of genus classification based on the species considered.

جنس قريب
جنس بعيد
جنس وسط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the 'middle' genus for 'human'?
A) Substance
B) Animal
C) Growing
D) Body

Key Takeaway
The threefold division of genus reveals that classification is relative—the same genus can be near, distant, or middle depending on the species.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the species 'date palm' (نخل). Identify its near genus (e.g., 'tree' شجر), distant genus (e.g., 'substance' جوهر), and any middle genera (e.g., 'plant' نبات). Explain how the same middle genus might be near for a different species.
?
Select a species from fiqh (e.g., 'grapes' عنب) and determine its near, distant, and middle genera in the context of defining 'intoxicant' (مسكر) for legal rulings. Reflect on how the classification shifts if the species changes.

Near and Distant Differentia: Two Definitions
Two competing definitions of near and distant differentia

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between al-Katibi's definition of near and distant differentia and the alternative definition, and apply each to examples from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Differentia divides into near and distant, but there are two competing definitions—one based on genus hierarchy, the other on composition.

This lesson unpacks a key distinction in the theory of definition: the division of differentia (fasl) into near and distant. The commentator presents two competing methods—al-Katibi's, which uses proximity to the species' genus, and another that defines near differentia as the complete distinguisher and distant as a part of it. Understanding both is essential for evaluating definitions in the Islamic sciences, where precise differentiae determine the scope of rulings and classifications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of near differentia
Al-Katibi: the differentia that distinguishes the species from its near genus (e.g., 'rational' for human, whose near genus is 'animal'). Others: the complete distinguisher (tamām al-mumayyiz), which fully separates the species from everything else.
These definitions are not contradictory but operate on different principles: one focuses on the genus level, the other on the distinguishing power of the differentia itself.
2
Identify the two definitions of distant differentia
Al-Katibi: the differentia of the genus (e.g., 'sentient' for human, because it distinguishes 'animal' from 'plant'). Others: a part of the complete distinguisher (e.g., if 'rational' is composite, its own differentia is distant from human).
The distant differentia is less specific and does not fully distinguish the species from all others.
3
Apply al-Katibi's method to a new example
Take a species from fiqh: 'prayer' (salat). Its near genus is 'physical worship' (ibada badaniyya). The near differentia specifies the type of worship—e.g., 'with specific actions and recitations'. The distant differentia would be the differentia of 'physical worship' itself, e.g., 'involving bodily movements'.
This method relies on the genus-species hierarchy: the near differentia is at the same level as the species, while the distant is one genus higher.
4
Apply the alternative method to the same example
The complete distinguisher for 'prayer' would be the full set of properties that uniquely identify it. If we suppose that 'specific actions and recitations' is composite (e.g., 'standing, bowing, prostrating, reciting Al-Fatiha'), then each component is a part of the complete distinguisher. The near differentia is the entire composite; the distant differentia is a part (e.g., 'standing').
This method treats differentia as potentially composite, breaking it down into sub-differentiae.
5
Recognize the division's foundations
Al-Bajuri notes that the division into near and distant properly applies to 'differentia of existence' (fasl al-wujūd)—the differentia that distinguishes an essence from others sharing in existence—not to 'differentia of genus'. This distinction becomes important when dealing with composite essences.
The differentia of existence leads to the concept of co-extensive parts and degrees of distance, which must terminate to avoid infinite regress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كما يأتي . قوله : كَمَا لَوْ قَدَّرْتَ أَنَّ النَّاطِقَ مُرَكَّبٌ مِنْ جِنْسِ وَفَضْلٍ أي : كالعاقل والمتفكر، وفيه نظر؛ إذ لا يمكن أن يكون للفصل جنس ؛ إذ لو كان للفصل جنس، لكان ذلك الجنس جزءاً مِنَ لهم هذه المسألة أنَّ المقسم إلى القريب والبعيد فصل الوجود، لا فصل الجنس، وفصل الوجود أحد جزأي الحقيقة المركَّبة من أمرين متساويين، فكلُّ مِنَ الجزأين فصل الوجود؛ لأنَّه ميّزها عما يشاركها في الوجود، وهذا بناء على جواز تركيب الماهية من أمرين متساويين، كما إذا فرضنا أنَّ الإنسان تركَّب من متساويين : النَّاطق والضَّاحك ؛ إذ لا شك في مساواتهما للإنسان، وكلاهما مساو للآخر، لا أعم ولا أخصّ، فكلاهما فصل قريب له فإن فرضنا : أنَّ الناطق تركَّب من متساويين العاقل والمتفكّر، وتركب المتفكّر أيضاً مِنَ الذَّكيِّ والمتفطّن، فيكون المتفطن فصلاً قريباً للمتفكّر ، وفصل فصل للناطق بعيداً بمرتبة، وفصل فصل فصل للإنسان بعيداً ،بمرتبتين والمتفكّر قريباً للناطق بعيداً مِنَ الإنسان ،بمرتبة والناطق قريباً لا غير، وبتعدد الإضافة تُزادُ مراتب البعد ولا بد أن تنتهي إلى تمام المميز في بعض الفصول ؛ لئلا يتسلسل .
Note: Just as genus divides into near and distant, so too differentia: it is near, and it is the differentia of the species from its near genus, like 'rational' for 'human'. Bajuri's note: His statement: 'differentia of the species' means the differentia distinguishing the species from its partners in the near genus. His statement: 'like 'rational' for 'human'' means like 'rational' separating the essence of human from its partners in its near genus, which is 'animal', for 'rational' is the differentia of the species; i.e., it distinguishes it from its partners in its near genus which is 'animal' encompassing human and others. And it is distant, and it is the differentia of the genus, like 'sentient' for 'animal'. This is the method of al-Katibi. The well-known for others is that the near differentia is the complete distinguisher, like 'rational' for 'human', and the distant is a part of the complete distinguisher, as if you suppose that 'rational' is composed of a genus and a differentia, then the differentia of 'rational' is near to it, and distant from 'human'. Bajuri's note: His statement: 'like 'sentient' for 'animal'' means like 'sentient' separating the essence of human from its partners in its distant genus which is 'growing', for 'sentient' is the differentia of the essence of 'human' from its partners in its distant genus which is 'growing' encompassing animal and plant, and it is distant from human because it is the differentia of its genus, and complete distinction of the essence is not attained by it, but it distinguishes it from that which does not share it, like distinguishing human by sensation, for example, from tree and stone and the like, not from horse and bird. His statement: 'This is the method of al-Katibi' i.e., the author of 'al-Shamsiyya', and Sa'd al-Din followed him in 'al-Tahdhib', and it is correct as will come. His statement: 'as if you suppose that 'rational' is composed of a genus and a differentia' means like 'intelligent' and 'thoughtful', and there is consideration in it, for it is not possible for differentia to have a genus, for if differentia had a genus, that genus would be a part of the differentia, and nothing of the parts of the genus is included in the differentia, otherwise the aggregate would not be a differentia, but rather the differentia in reality is the last part. And also: supposing 'rational' composed of a genus and a differentia makes it a species, while the assumption is that it is a differentia, and the well-known to them is that what is divided into near and distant is differentia of existence, not differentia of genus, and differentia of existence is one of the two parts of the essence composed of two co-extensive things, so each of the two parts is a differentia of existence because it distinguishes the essence from what shares it in existence, and this is based on the permissibility of composition of essence from two co-extensive things, as if we suppose that human is composed of two co-extensives: 'rational' and 'laughing', for there is no doubt they are co-extensive to human, and both are co-extensive to each other, neither more general nor more specific, so both are near differentiae for it. For if we suppose that 'rational' is composed of two co-extensives 'intelligent' and 'thoughtful', and 'thoughtful' is also composed of 'clever' and 'perceptive', then 'perceptive' is a near differentia for 'thoughtful', and a differentia of differentia for 'rational' distant by one degree, and a differentia of differentia of differentia for 'human' distant by two degrees, and 'thoughtful' is near for 'rational' distant from 'human' by one degree, and 'rational' is near only, and with multiplicity of relation the degrees of distance increase, and it must terminate at the complete distinguisher in some differentiae to prevent infinite regress.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion covering the division of differentia (fasl) into near and distant, along with two competing definitions. The commentator first notes that just as genus divides, so does differentia. The near differentia is that which distinguishes the species from its near genus (e.g., 'rational' for human). The distant differentia is that which distinguishes the genus itself (e.g., 'sentient' for animal). This is al-Katibi's method. The other common method defines the near differentia as the complete distinguisher (tamām al-mumayyiz) and the distant as a part of that complete distinguisher. The commentator gives an example: if 'rational' is composed of a genus and a differentia, then the differentia of 'rational' is near to 'rational' but distant from 'human'. Al-Bajuri (via the marginal note) then critiques this: differentia cannot have a genus because that would make the differentia a species. He explains that the division into near and distant actually applies to 'differentia of existence' (fasl al-wujūd), which is one of two co-extensive parts of an essence. He illustrates with the decomposition of 'rational' into 'intelligent' and 'thoughtful', showing how degrees of distance are generated. The passage ends with the warning that this decomposition must terminate to avoid infinite regress.

Key Terms
فصل قريب
فصل بعيد
فصل الوجود
تمام المميز

Key Takeaway
The division of differentia into near and distant is understood in two ways: one based on the genus hierarchy (al-Katibi) and one based on the composition of the complete distinguisher (others), both of which are used in the Islamic sciences to refine definitions.

Four Ranks of Genus and the Role of Differentia
Author enumerates four ranks of genus and explains the necessary relation of differentia to each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the four ranks of genus (high, low, intermediate, isolated) and determine whether each requires a constitutive differentia, a divisive differentia, both, or none.

Core Idea
A genus's rank dictates the type of differentia it must have.

In this passage, the author divides genus into four ranks and explains how the differentia functions differently for each. The high genus has only a divisive differentia, the low species only a constitutive one, and intermediate genera/species require both. Additionally, the passage clarifies the dual role of a single differentia: it is constitutive for its own species and divisive for the higher genus. Understanding these relations is essential for constructing precise definitions in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four ranks
Locate the Arabic list: عَالٍ، وَسَافِلِ، وَمُتَوَسِّط، و منفرد. These are the four ranks of genus.
The isolated rank (منفرد) is mentioned but not elaborated in this passage.
2
Extract the definition of high genus
Find the description for high genus: الَّذِي لَا جِنْسَ فَوْقَهُ، وَتَحْتَهُ الأَجْنَاسُ. This defines it as having no genus above and having genera below.
It is also called 'جنس الأجناس' (genus of genera).
3
Understand the differentia requirements from the tanbih
Read the section starting with 'تنبية' to see the necessary differentia for each rank: high genus needs a divisive differentia, low species needs a constitutive differentia, intermediate needs both.
This section also provides the example of 'rational' to illustrate the dual role.
4
Apply the example of 'rational'
Note that 'rational' is constitutive for 'man' (it defines his essence) and divisive for 'animal' (it creates a species under animal).
This shows how one differentia can have two roles depending on what it is related to.
5
Determine the differentia for each rank
Based on the text: high genus requires only a divisive differentia; low species requires only a constitutive differentia; intermediate requires both a constitutive and a divisive differentia.
The isolated rank is not discussed and may have no differentia.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) - التَّقْسِيمُ الثَّانِي لِلجِنْسِ : أَنَّهُمْ ذَكَرُوا لَهُ أَرْبَعَ مَرَاتِبَ : عَالٍ، وَسَافِلِ، وَمُتَوَسِّط، و منفرد . ۱ - فَالجِنْسُ العَالِي هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا جِنْسَ فَوْقَهُ، وَتَحْتَهُ الأَجْنَاسُ، وَيُسَمَّى: (جِنْسَ الأَجْنَاسِ). قوله : (وَكَذَا لَوْ قَدَّرْتَ فيه نظر؛ إذ لا يمكن أن يكون للفصل جنس كما تقدم. قوله : (وَهَذِهِ أُمُورٌ تَقْدِيرِيَّةٌ ... إلخ) أي : لأنَّ الفصل المميز في الوجود ليس محقق الوجود، بل هو مبني على احتمال يذكر، ولأجل ذلك عدل الكاتبيُّ عن هذا الاصطلاح إلى الأوَّل، وجعل التقسيم في فصل الجنس الذي هو موجود قطعاً، وهو ما يفصل الشَّيء عن جنس؛ سواء كان المفصول به جنساً أو نوعاً، ولذا ينقسم إلى فصل النّوع إن كان المفصول به نوعاً حقيقياً ك: «النَّاطق»، وفصل جنس إن كان المفصول به جنساً كـ «الحسّاس» بهذا الاعتبار. والَّذي غرَّ هذا الشَّارح حتّى جعل للفصل جنساً ظاهرُ كلام السَّنوسي، مع أنَّه إن حمل كلام السنوسي على ذلك لا يلتئم كلامه، كما يُعلم بالوقوف عليه. تنبية: إذا نُسِب الفصل إلى ما يميزه فهو مقوّم له ، أو إلى ما ميّز عنه فهو مقسم؛ مثلاً: «الناطق» فصل ميز «الإنسان» عن «الحيوان المشترك بينه وبين غيره، فالنَّاطق مقوّم للإنسان؛ أي: داخل في قوامه ؛ أي: حقيقته ؛ لأنَّه جزؤها الذي تقومت به؛ أي: تركَّبت منه ، وهو ـ أعني : «الناطق» - مقسم للحَيَوَان ؛ أي: محصل لقسم منه ؛ لأنَّه محصل للإنسان، وهو قسمٌ مِنَ الحَيوان، فالجنس العالي يجب أن يكون له فصل يقسمه ؛ ضرورة أنَّ تحته الأنواع الإضافية والحقيقية، ولا يجوز أن يكون له فصل يقومه ؛ إذ لا جنس فوقه . والنَّوعُ السَّافل يجب أن يكون له فصل يقومه ؛ ضرورةً اندراجه تحت جنس، ولا يجوز أن يكون له فصل يقسمه ؛ ضرورة أنَّه لا نوع تحته والمتوسط مِنَ الأنواع والأجناس يجب أن يكون له فصل مقوم وفصل مقسم .
(2) The second division of the genus: that they mentioned for it four ranks: high, low, intermediate, and isolated. 1. The high genus is that which has no genus above it, and below it are genera, and it is called 'genus of genera'. He said: (And likewise if you supposed... there is consideration in it; because it is impossible for a differentia to have a genus, as previously mentioned). He said: (And these are hypothetical matters... etc.) meaning: because the differentia that distinguishes in existence is not actualized existence, but is based on a probability mentioned, and for that reason al-Katibi turned away from this terminology to the first, and made the division in the differentia of the genus which is certainly existing, and it is what separates a thing from its genus, whether the separated thing is a genus or a species, and therefore it is divided into differentia of the species if the separated thing is a real species, like 'rational', and differentia of the genus if the separated thing is a genus, like 'sentient' from this perspective. What deceived this commentator until he gave the differentia a genus is the apparent meaning of al-Sanusi's words, but if al-Sanusi's words are interpreted in that way, his speech would not be coherent, as is known by examining it. Warning: When the differentia is related to what it distinguishes, it is constitutive of it, or to what it distinguishes from, it is divisive; for example: 'rational' is a differentia that distinguishes 'man' from 'animal' common between him and others, so 'rational' is constitutive of man; i.e., it is part of his constitution; i.e., his essence; because it is the part by which he is constituted; i.e., composed of, and it — namely 'rational' — is a divisor of 'animal'; i.e., it obtains a section of it; because it obtains man, and he is a section of animal. So the high genus must have a differentia that divides it; necessarily because below it are relative and real species, and it is not permissible to have a differentia that constitutes it, since there is no genus above it. The low species must have a differentia that constitutes it; necessarily because it falls under a genus, and it is not permissible to have a differentia that divides it; necessarily because there is no species below it. The intermediate among species and genera must have a constitutive differentia and a divisive differentia.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage presents the second division of the genus into four ranks: high, low, intermediate, and isolated. The high genus is defined as that which has no genus above it and has genera below it, also called 'genus of genera'. The commentator then returns to a previous issue: al-Katibi's preference for the first division of differentia into near and far based on existing differentia of the genus, avoiding hypothetical constructions. Al-Katibi's differentia of the genus is actual, and it can be either a differentia of a species (like 'rational') or a differentia of a genus (like 'sentient'), depending on what it distinguishes. The commentator criticizes an unnamed commentator (probably the author of the main commentary) for mistakenly inferring that a differentia can have a genus from al-Sanusi's words. Then comes a 'warning' (tanbih) that explains the two roles of a differentia: when related to the thing it distinguishes, it is constitutive (muqawwim); when related to the genus from which it distinguishes, it is divisive (muqassim). Using the example of 'rational' for 'man' vs. 'animal', the passage clarifies that a high genus (like 'animal') must have a divisive differentia (to create species under it), while a low species (like 'man') must have a constitutive differentia (to define its essence). Intermediate types require both a constitutive and a divisive differentia. This passage ties the classification of genera to the functional role of differentiae.

جنس عال
جنس سافل
فصل مقوم

The rank of a genus determines whether its differentia is constitutive, divisive, or both.

8 min
The Four Ranks of Genus
Author defines the four ranks of genus with examples from the hierarchy of jins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four ranks of genus (high, low, intermediate, isolated) in a hierarchy of universals and explain why terms like 'existent' and 'thing' are not considered genera.

Core Idea
Genus is defined by its position in the hierarchy: high has none above, low has none below, intermediate has both, isolated has neither.

In Islamic logic, the classification of genus into four ranks helps clarify the structure of definitions. This passage from Bajuri's commentary presents these ranks with examples from the standard hierarchy beginning with 'substance'. Understanding this classification is essential for constructing accurate definitions (hadd) and avoiding common errors where accidental universals are mistaken for genera.

Guided Path
1
Understand the criterion for each rank
The key is the presence or absence of a genus above and below. High: no genus above, genera below. Low: no genus below, species below. Intermediate: both a genus above and a genus below. Isolated: neither above nor below.
2
Apply the criterion to 'substance'
Identify why 'substance' is high: it has no genus above it, and it has 'body', 'growing', 'animal' as genera below.
This makes it the 'genus of genera'.
3
Apply to 'animal' as low genus
Note that 'animal' has no genus below; its subordinates are species like 'human' and 'horse'.
4
Apply to 'body' as intermediate
Body has 'substance' above and 'animal' below.
5
Test the borderline: 'existent'
Although 'existent' is broader than 'substance', it is not a genus because it is not part of the essence of substance; it is an accident. Therefore, it does not qualify as a genus.
This illustrates that extension alone does not determine genus; essential predication is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التَّقْسِيمُ الثَّانِي لِلجِنْسِ : أَنَّهُمْ ذَكَرُوا لَهُ أَرْبَعَ مَرَاتِبَ : عَالٍ، وَسَافِلِ، وَمُتَوَسِّط، وَمُنْفَرِد. فَالجِنْسُ العَالِي هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا جِنْسَ فَوْقَهُ، وَتَحْتَهُ الأَجْنَاسُ، وَيُسَمَّى: (جِنْسَ الأَجْنَاسِ) [ / ١٤] ـ : ((الجَوْهَرِ ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا جِنْسَ فَوْقَهُ وَتَحْتَهُ أَجْنَاسٌ كَـ «الجِسْمِ))، وَ: «النَّامِي))، وَ: «الحَيَوَانِ). وَأَمَّا الحَادِثُ وَ: «المَوْجُودُ وَ : «الشَّيْءُ»، فَإِنَّهَا وَإِنْ كَانَتْ أَعَمُّ مِنَ الجَوْهَرِ»، لَكِنْ لَيْسَ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهَا بِجِنْسِ لَهُ ؛ لِخُرُوجِهَا عَنِ مَاهِيَتِهِ ، وَقَدْ عَدُّوهَا مِنْ لَوَزَامِ الوُجُودِ لا المَاهِيَّةِ ، فَهِيَ كُلُّهَا مِنَ العَرَضِيَّاتِ، فَلِذَا لَمْ يَذْكُرُوهَا. ٢ - وَالجِنْسُ السَّافِلُ هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا جِنْسَ تَحْتَهُ كَـ: «الحَيَوَانِ»، فَإِنَّهُ لَا جِنْسَ تَحْتَهُ، وَإِنَّمَا تَحْتَهُ الأَنْوَاعُ كَـ : الإِنْسَانِ وَ : «الفَرَسِ»، وَفَوْقَهُ الأَجْنَاسُ . ٣ - وَالجِنْسُ المُتَوَسِّطُ هُوَ : الَّذِي فَوْقَهُ جِنْسٍ وَتَحْتَهُ جِنْسٌ گـ: «الجِسْمِ فَوْقَهُ الجَوْهَرُ» ، وَتَحْتَهُ الحَيَوَانُ). ٤ - وَالمُنْفَرِدُ هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا جِنْسَ فَوْقَهُ وَلَا جِنْسَ تَحْتَهُ ؛
The second division of genus: they mentioned for it four ranks: high, low, intermediate, and isolated. The high genus is that which has no genus above it and below it are genera, and it is called 'the genus of genera' – like 'substance', for it has no genus above it and below it are genera such as 'body', 'growing', and 'animal'. As for 'accident', 'existent', and 'thing', even though they are more general than 'substance', none of them is a genus for it because they exit from its essence, and they counted them among the concomitants of existence not of essence, so they are all accidents, therefore they did not mention them. 2. The low genus is that which has no genus below it, like 'animal', for there is no genus below it, only below it are species like 'human' and 'horse', and above it are genera. 3. The intermediate genus is that which has a genus above it and a genus below it, like 'body' – above it is 'substance' and below it is 'animal'. 4. The isolated genus is that which has no genus above it nor below it.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage presents the second classification of genus (jins), dividing it into four ranks based on its position in the hierarchy of universals. The classification is definitional, providing a clear criterion for each rank along with examples. The author begins by stating that scholars have enumerated four ranks: high (ʿālī), low (sāfil), intermediate (mutawassiṭ), and isolated (munfarid). Then each is defined.

1. The high genus (al-jins al-ʿālī) is that which has no genus above it and has genera below it. It is also called 'genus of genera' (jins al-ajnās). The example given is 'substance' (jawhar), which is the highest genus in the category of substance; above it there is no genus, and below it are genera such as 'body' (jism), 'growing' (nāmī), and 'animal' (ḥayawān). The author then clarifies why certain universal concepts like 'accident' (ḥādith), 'existent' (mawjūd), and 'thing' (shayʾ) are not considered genera for substance, even though they are more general. The reason is that they are not part of the essence (māhiyya) of substance but are accidents (ʿaraḍiyyāt) – concomitants of existence, not of quiddity. Hence they are not included in the hierarchy of genera.

2. The low genus (al-jins al-sāfil) is that which has no genus below it. The example is 'animal' (ḥayawān), which is a genus for species like 'human' (insān) and 'horse' (faras), but there is no genus beneath it; instead, its subordinates are species.

3. The intermediate genus (al-jins al-mutawassiṭ) is that which has a genus above it and a genus below it. The example is 'body' (jism), which has 'substance' above it and 'animal' below it.

4. The isolated genus (al-jins al-munfarid) is that which has no genus above it nor below it. This is a special case; in the commentary it is noted that some objected to including this rank because it has no relation of generality or specificity to others, and the discussion is about ranks in a series.

The passage is clear and uses standard examples from the logical tradition, particularly from the genus 'substance' downward. All examples are from the Islamic sciences (substance, body, animal, human, horse) and are rooted in the Aristotelian classification adopted by Muslim logicians.

Key Terms

جنس عال
جنس سافل
جنس متوسط
جنس منفرد

Checkpoint

A) 'Substance' (jawhar)
B) 'Animal' (ḥayawān)
C) 'Body' (jism)
D) 'Human' (insān)

Key Takeaway
The four ranks of genus are determined solely by their position relative to other genera in the hierarchy, not by their extension alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Three Remaining Divisions of Genus: Lowest, Middle, and Isolated
Author defines the four types of genus: highest, lowest, middle, and isolated, with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given genus as highest, lowest, middle, or isolated based on its position in the hierarchy of genera and species.

Core Idea
Genus is defined by its relatives: above, below, or both.

In the previous lesson we learned about the highest genus, which has no genus above it. Now we turn to the remaining three divisions: the lowest, the middle, and the isolated. These categories help us understand how concepts relate to one another in a hierarchical structure. By mastering them, you will be able to map the relationships between terms in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the highest and lowest extremes
First, recall that the highest genus has no genus above it; the lowest genus has no genus beneath it (only species). For a given candidate, ask: Is there a broader category above it? Is there a narrower category beneath it that is still a genus?
For example, 'animal' (hayawan) has species like human and horse beneath it, but no genus beneath it, so it is lowest.
2
Test for middle genus
A middle genus has both a genus above and a genus below. Check if the candidate is a species of a higher genus and also a genus for something lower. For instance, 'body' (jism) is a species of 'substance' (jawhar) and a genus for 'animal' (hayawan).
If both conditions are met, it is a middle genus.
3
Check for isolated genus
An isolated genus has no genus above and no genus below. This is a controversial category. Examine whether the candidate truly has no broader category and no narrower genus (only species). If so, it is isolated.
The passage gives no example; later scholars debate whether such a category exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالجِنْسُ السَّافِلُ هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا جِنْسَ تَحْتَهُ كَـ: «الحَيَوَانِ»، فَإِنَّهُ لَا جِنْسَ تَحْتَهُ، وَإِنَّمَا تَحْتَهُ الأَنْوَاعُ كَـ : الإِنْسَانِ وَ : «الفَرَسِ»، وَفَوْقَهُ الأَجْنَاسُ . - وَالجِنْسُ المُتَوَسِّطُ هُوَ : الَّذِي فَوْقَهُ جِنْسِ وَتَحْتَهُ جِنْسٌ گـ: «الجِسْمِ فَوْقَهُ الجَوْهَرُ» ، وَتَحْتَهُ الحَيَوَانُ). - وَالمُنْفَرِدُ هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا جِنْسَ فَوْقَهُ وَلَا جِنْسَ تَحْتَهُ ؛
The lowest genus is that which has no genus beneath it, like 'al-hayawan' (animal). It has no genus beneath it; only species beneath it like 'al-insan' (human) and 'al-faras' (horse), and above it are genera. The middle genus is that which has a genus above it and a genus beneath it, like 'al-jism' (body): above it is 'al-jawhar' (substance), and beneath it is 'al-hayawan' (animal). The isolated genus is that which has no genus above it and no genus beneath it.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a definitional passage that divides genera into three types (the fourth, the highest, was mentioned earlier in the text). The lowest genus (al-jins al-safil) is one that has no other genus below it, only species. The example given is 'al-hayawan' (animal): it is not a genus for anything else, but it is a genus for humans and horses. Above it lie higher genera like 'jism' (body) and 'jawhar' (substance). The middle genus (al-jins al-mutawassit) has both a genus above and a genus below. The example is 'al-jism' (body): above it is 'jawhar' (substance), below it is 'al-hayawan' (animal). The isolated genus (al-munfarid) is one that has no genus above nor below. This classification helps in understanding the hierarchy of reality and the relationships between concepts in logic.

Key Terms
الجنس السافل
الجنس المتوسط
المنفرد

Key Takeaway
The three additional types of genus—lowest, middle, and isolated—complete the classification based on hierarchical position.

Objection to the Isolated Genus and Its Defense
Commentator records and responds to an objection about the isolated genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the objection against including the isolated genus in the classification of genera and explain the commentator's defense based on ordering by negation.

Core Idea
The isolated genus is retained not by positive relation, but by negation.

In this passage, al-Bajuri records an objection against including the isolated genus in the classification of genera, since it has no hierarchical relation to others. He then defends its inclusion by showing that the classification can be extended by considering a negative criterion. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to evaluate complete classifications in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What is the objector's complaint? Why should the isolated genus be dropped? The objector says there is no relation of generality or specificity between the isolated genus and other genera, and the topic is about hierarchical levels, so the isolated does not fit.
2
Analyze the classification of genera
List the four types of genus from the passage: the highest (most general), the lowest (most specific), the middle (more general than some and more specific than others), and the isolated (completely separate). How does each fit into a hierarchy?
The isolated is defined by having no relation at all.
3
Understand the defense
How does the commentator justify keeping the isolated genus? What role does negation play? The answer says 'the ordering in it is on the basis of negation' – meaning the isolated genus is classified precisely because it lacks both higher and lower genera. This negative criterion makes the division exhaustive.
The same reasoning applies to an isolated species.
4
Apply the principle
Consider the note that an example of an isolated genus is impossible (mut'adhdhir) according to Ahl al-Haqq. Why? Because the ten categories (al-ajnas al-'ashara) all have a genus beneath them (i.e., species). The isolated genus remains a theoretical possibility with no actual instance.
This shows that logical categories can be defined even when no real example exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعترض بعضُهم ذكر هذا القسم وقال : الصَّوابُ إسقاطه؛ لأنَّه لا نسبة بينه وبين غيره بعموم ولا خصوص، والكلام في بيان المراتب، والمنفرد ليس واقعاً في سلسلة الترتيب. وبيان ذلك أنَّ الجنس إمَّا أعمُّ الأجناس وهو العالي، ويسمى : جنس الأجناس، وإما أخصُّ وهو السافل ولا يسمى: «جنس الأجناس»، خلافاً لقدورة، وإمَّا أعم من بعض وأخصُّ مِن بعض، وهو المتوسط ، أو مباين للكلِّ، وهو المنفرد، فقدِ اتَّضح أنَّه لا نسبة بينه وبين غيره. وقد يجاب : بأنَّهم إنَّما ذكروه نظراً إلى أنَّ التَّرتيب فيه باعتبار النفي، فتأمله . ومثل ما ورد هنا يَرِدُ في النوع المنفرد. قوله : (وَمِثَالُهُ مُتَعَذِّرٌ) أي: على مذهب أهل الحقِّ؛ لأنَّ الأجناس العشرة التي ظفرت بها الفلاسفة كلُّها تحتها جنس، وغيرها لم يقم دليل على وجوده ولا على عدمه
Some objected to the mention of this division and said: The correct is to drop it, because there is no relation between it and others by generality or specificity, and the discussion concerns the clarification of levels, and the isolated is not placed in the chain of ordering. The explanation of that is: The genus is either the most general of genera, which is the highest, and is called the genus of genera; or the most specific, which is the lowest, and is not called 'genus of genera', contrary to Qudura; or it is more general than some and more specific than some, which is the middle; or it is completely separate, which is the isolated. So it is clear that there is no relation between it and others. And it may be answered: They only mentioned it considering that the ordering in it is on the basis of negation, so ponder. And the same objection occurs for the isolated species. His statement: 'Its example is impossible' means according to the doctrine of the people of truth, because the ten genera that the philosophers obtained all have a genus beneath them, and no proof has been established for the existence or non-existence of others.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange: an objection and its answer regarding the inclusion of the isolated genus in the classification. The objector argues that the isolated genus should be removed because it has no proportional relation (no generality or specificity) with others, and since the topic is about hierarchical levels, the isolated genus does not fit. The commentator then explains that the classification actually enumerates four possibilities: most general (highest), most specific (lowest), intermediate (middle), and completely different (isolated). The isolated is defined by negation (neither above nor below). The answer defends inclusion by saying the classification uses the criterion of negation rather than positive relations. It also notes that an actual example of an isolated genus is impossible (mut'adhdhir) in the real world, according to the 'people of truth' (ahl al-haqq), because all ten known categories have a genus above or below. Thus, the isolated genus remains a theoretical possibility but has no actual instance. The same objection applies to an isolated species.

Key Terms
المنفرد
النفي
الأجناس العشرة

Key Takeaway
The isolated genus is a logical category defined by negation; it completes the division of genera even though no actual instance exists.

Conceptual Distinction of Near and Far Genus
Author defines near and far genus conceptually.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define near genus and far genus in conceptual terms and distinguish them based on the criterion of commonality.

Core Idea
Genus nearness is about conceptual scope: near genus is the full commonality, far genus includes higher categories.

In Islamic logic, genera are not fixed; they are relative to the species under consideration. The author explains that the difference between near and far genus is not just a matter of hierarchy but of conceptual content. Near genus captures the entire common essence shared by a quiddity and its peers, while far genus is a broader category with additional subgenera.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key definitions
Find the definition of near genus ('tamm al-mushtarak') and lower/far genus ('jins saafil') in the text. Near genus is defined as the entire commonality between a quiddity and every quiddity that shares with it. Lower genus is defined as that which has no genus below it and has a genus above it.
These definitions are purely conceptual, not yet applied to examples.
2
Compare the definitions
Notice that near genus is defined by full commonality, while lower genus is defined by its position in the hierarchy (no genus below it). The near genus is immediate to the species, whereas the far genus is broader and more remote.
The contrast highlights that nearness is about the extent of commonality, not just distance in a chain.
3
Understand the conceptual difference
The conceptual difference (maghayira fi al-mafhum) lies in the scope of commonality. Near genus is the full commonality shared by a quiddity and all its equals under the same genus. Far genus (like absolute body) is a higher genera that includes additional differentiating features below it.
This distinction is crucial for accurate definitions in Islamic sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مباحث الألفاظ وقد علمت المغايرة بينهما مفهوما ومصدوقا. قصارة. أما المغايرة في المفهوم : فلأنَّ الجنس القريب على الأوّل هو تمام المشترك بين الماهية وبين كلّ ماهية تشاركها فيه، والسافل هو الذي لا جنس تحته وفوقه جنس وأمَّا مصدوقاً : فالجسمُ النَّامي فإنَّه على التقسيم الأوّل جنس قريب بالنسبة إلى النبات; لأنَّه تمام المشترك بينه وبين كلّ ما يشاركه فيه بخلافه على الثَّاني، فهو جنس وسط; لأنَّ فوقه جنس وهو الجسم المطلق، وتحته جنس وهو الحيوان.
Section on Investigations of Expressions. You have already known the difference between them in concept and in actuality. (Marginal note). As for the difference in concept: because the near genus is, in the first division, the entire commonality between the quiddity and every quiddity that shares with it, and the lower genus is that which has no genus below it and has a genus above it. As for in actuality: the growing body (jism al-nami) - according to the first division it is a near genus with respect to 'plant', because it is the entire commonality between it and everything that shares with it; differently in the second division, it is a middle genus, because above it is a genus which is absolute body, and below it is a genus which is animal.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is a definitional explanation of the distinction between near (qarib) and far (ba'id) genus, both in concept (mafhum) and in actuality (masduq). In concept, the near genus is the entire commonality shared by a quiddity and others that share with it; the lower genus (saafil) is that which has no genus below it and has a genus above it. In actuality, the author gives the example of 'growing body' (jism al-nami). According to the first classification, 'growing body' is a near genus relative to 'plant' because it fully captures what is common among plants. According to the second classification, 'growing body' is a middle genus because it has 'absolute body' above it and 'animal' below it. This illustrates how the same item can be considered near or far depending on the classification system.

Key Terms
جنس قريب
جنس سافل
تمام المشترك
جسم نامي

Key Takeaway
Near genus is the immediate common essence; far genus is a broader category with subgenera.

Genus Relativity: The Example of Growing Body
Author uses 'growing body' to illustrate genus relativity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of genus relativity by determining the classification of 'growing body' in different divisions.

Core Idea
The same quiddity can be near, middle, or far genus depending on the classification system.

The author uses the example of 'growing body' (jism al-nami) to show that genus classification is relative. In one division (first classification), it is a near genus relative to 'plant'. In another division (second classification), it is a middle genus with a genus above ('absolute body') and a genus below ('animal'). This illustrates that the nearness of a genus is not absolute but depends on the perspective of the classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the example and its two classifications
Locate 'growing body' (jism al-nami) in the text. The author discusses it under two divisions: first division and second division. Notice that the example is used to demonstrate the distinction in actuality (masduq).
The 'first division' refers to the conceptual definition of near genus; the 'second division' is a different taxonomic perspective.
2
Analyze the first classification
In the first division, 'growing body' is a near genus relative to 'plant' because it is the entire commonality between plant and everything that shares that commonality. It captures all that is essential for being a growing body.
Here, 'plant' is a species under 'growing body'.
3
Analyze the second classification
In the second division, 'growing body' becomes a middle genus. Above it is 'absolute body' (jism mutlaq) which is a far genus, and below it is 'animal' which is a lower genus. This means 'growing body' is not the most specific or the most general; it sits in between.
The second division reveals a hierarchy: absolute body > growing body > animal.
4
Understand genus relativity
Recognize that the same item (growing body) can be a near genus in one classification and a middle genus in another. This shows that genus roles are relative to the chosen division and the species under consideration.
This relativity is crucial for correctly applying definitions in Islamic sciences, where the same term may function differently in different contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مباحث الألفاظ وقد علمت المغايرة بينهما مفهوما ومصدوقا. قصارة. أما المغايرة في المفهوم : فلأنَّ الجنس القريب على الأوّل هو تمام المشترك بين الماهية وبين كلّ ماهية تشاركها فيه، والسافل هو الذي لا جنس تحته وفوقه جنس وأمَّا مصدوقاً : فالجسمُ النَّامي فإنَّه على التقسيم الأوّل جنس قريب بالنسبة إلى النبات; لأنَّه تمام المشترك بينه وبين كلّ ما يشاركه فيه بخلافه على الثَّاني، فهو جنس وسط; لأنَّ فوقه جنس وهو الجسم المطلق، وتحته جنس وهو الحيوان.
Section on Investigations of Expressions. You have already known the difference between them in concept and in actuality. (Marginal note). As for the difference in concept: because the near genus is, in the first division, the entire commonality between the quiddity and every quiddity that shares with it, and the lower genus is that which has no genus below it and has a genus above it. As for in actuality: the growing body (jism al-nami) - according to the first division it is a near genus with respect to 'plant', because it is the entire commonality between it and everything that shares with it; differently in the second division, it is a middle genus, because above it is a genus which is absolute body, and below it is a genus which is animal.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is a definitional explanation of the distinction between near (qarib) and far (ba'id) genus, both in concept (mafhum) and in actuality (masduq). In concept, the near genus is the entire commonality shared by a quiddity and others that share with it; the lower genus (saafil) is that which has no genus below it and has a genus above it. In actuality, the author gives the example of 'growing body' (jism al-nami). According to the first classification, 'growing body' is a near genus relative to 'plant' because it fully captures what is common among plants. According to the second classification, 'growing body' is a middle genus because it has 'absolute body' above it and 'animal' below it. This illustrates how the same item can be considered near or far depending on the classification system.

Key Terms
جسم نامي
جسم مطلق
جنس قريب
جنس وسط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second division, what is the genus above 'growing body' (jism al-nami)?
A) Plant
B) Animal
C) Absolute body
D) Living being

Key Takeaway
Genus nearness is relative; the same item can be near, middle, or far genus depending on the classification division.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider 'animal' in relation to 'man' and 'horse'. Is animal a near or far genus for man? For horse? Explain using the concepts of first and second division from this lesson.
?
In usul al-fiqh, 'transaction' (bay') is a genus. If we say 'sale' is a species of transaction, is transaction a near or far genus relative to 'sale'? What would make it a middle genus? Construct a hierarchy.

The Four Ranks of Relative Species
Enumerating the four ranks of relative species and distinguishing them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the four ranks of relative species (low, high, intermediate, isolated) using examples from the Islamic logical tradition.

Core Idea
Relative species are hierarchically ordered; each rank depends on what species lies above or below it.

In this passage, Bajuri-Bannani enumerates the four ranks of relative species, mirroring the ranks of genus. This classification is crucial for understanding how definitions are structured and how species relate to genera in the Porphyrian tree. Pay close attention to the examples: human (low), body (high), animal (intermediate), and intellect (isolated).

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of ranking
The ranking of relative species depends on whether there is a species above or below it. The low species has none below; the high species has none above; the intermediate has both; the isolated has neither.
2
Define the low species (al-sāfil)
It is the most specific, with no species under it. Example: human (insān). It is called 'species of species'.
3
Define the high species (al-ʿālī)
It has no relative species above it, only genus. Example: body (jism), above which is only substance (jawhar).
4
Define the intermediate species (al-mutawassiṭ)
It has both a species above and below. Example: animal (ḥayawān): above is body, below is human.
5
Define the isolated species (al-munfarid)
It has no species above or below. Example: intellect (ʿaql) according to philosophers. Note: it may still have a genus above, so it is still a species.
Some logicians object to this classification; see the following lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَقَدْ عَلِمْتَ المُغَايَرَةَ بَيْنَهُمَا مَفْهُوماً وَمَصْدُوقاً أمَّا المغايرة في المفهوم : فلأنَّ الجنس القريب على الأوّل هو تمام المشترك بين الماهية وبين كلّ ماهية تشاركها فيه، والسافل هو الذي لا جنس تحته وفوقه جنس وأمَّا مصدوقاً : فالجسمُ النَّامي فإنَّه على التقسيم الأوّل جنس قريب بالنسبة إلى النبات; لأنَّه تمام المشترك بينه وبين كلّ ما يشاركه فيه بخلافه على الثَّاني، فهو جنس وسط; لأنَّ فوقه جنس وهو الجسم المطلق، وتحته جنس وهو الحيوان.
تنبيه:
كَمَا أَنَّ الجِنْسَ لَهُ مَرَاتِبٌ أَرْبَعٌ ، كَذَلِكَ النَّوْعُ الإِضَافِيُّ لَهُ مَرَاتِبُ أَرْبَعُ : 
١ - فَالنَّوْعُ السَّافِلُ هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا نَوْعَ تَحْتَهُ، وَيُسَمَّى: «نَوْعَ الأَنْوَاعِ»; لِأَنَّهُ نَوْعٌ مِنَ الأَنْوَاعِ الإِضَافِيَّةِ الَّتِي فَوْقَهُ كَـ: «الإِنْسَانِ».
٢ - وَالنَّوْعُ العَالِي هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا نَوْعٌ إِضَافِيٌّ فَوْقَهُ كَ: «الجِسْمِ»، فَإِنَّهُ لَيْسَ فَوْقَهُ إِلَّا الجِنْسَ العَالِي ، وَهُوَ الجَوْهَرُ.
٣ - وَالنَّوْعُ المُتَوَسِّطُ هُوَ الَّذِي فَوْقَهُ نَوْعٌ وَتَحْتَهُ نَوْعٌ كَـ: «الحَيَوَانِ» فَوْقَهُ الجِسْمُ، وَتَحْتَهُ الإِنْسَانُ.
٤ - وَالنَّوْعُ المُنْفَرِدُ هُوَ: الَّذِي لَا نَوْعَ فَوْقَهُ، وَلَا نَوْعَ تَحْتَهُ، وَمِثَالُهُ أَيْضاً مُتَعَذِّرٌ; إِلَّا أَنَّهُ مُثْلَ لَهُ بِالعَقْلِ عِنْدَ الفَلَاسِفَةِ، عَلَى قَوْلِ مَنْ قَالَ مِنْهُمْ : «إِنَّهُ نَوْعٌ، وَإِنَّهُ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ الجَوْهَرِ» كَمَا مَرَّ ، وَكَوْنُهُ لَا نَوْعَ فَوْقَهُ لَا يُنَافِي أَنَّ الجِنْسَ فَوْقَهُ ، فَبَطَلَ اعْتِرَاضُ مَنِ اعْتَرَضَ عَلَى المُمَثْلَيْنِ بِهِ، وَهَوَّلَ فِي ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ جَعْلَهُ مِنْ أَقْسَامِ الإِضَافِي يَسْتَلْزِمُ تَرْكِيبَهُ; لِانْدِارَجِهِ تَحْتَ جِنْسِ حَتْماً، مَعَ أَنَّ المُنْفَرِدَ غَيْرُ مُرَكَّبٍ .
قوله : (النَّوْعُ الإِضَافِيُّ) قال بعضهم : الصَّوابُ إسقاط هذا الوصف ; لأنَّ الأربع مراتب إنَّما هي لمطلق النوع; إذ النوع المنفرد ليس بإضافي، وهم جعلوه مِنَ الإضافي، وقد تبع الشارح فيه الهلالي التابع للسَّنوسي التّابع للخونجي، وقد اعترض هذه العبارة ابن مرزوق بما ذكرنا .
وإنما قيَّدوا النوع بـ «الإضافي» ; لأنَّ الأنواع الحقيقيَّة يستحيل أن تترتب; لأنَّ النَّوع الحقيقيَّ لا يكون نوع آخر فوقه حقيقي، وإلا لكان النّوع الحقيقي جنساً بخلاف الأنواع الإضافية، فيجوز أن يكون نوعٌ إضافي فوقه نوع آخر إضافي; إذ لا منع .
قوله : (وَإِنَّهُ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ الجَوْهَرِ ) أي : فيكون الجوهر جنساً له; يقال عليه وعلى غيره في جواب «ما هو؟»، وتكون العقول العشرة أفراداً له لا أنواعاً حتّى يتحقق تحته نوع آخر .
قوله : (فَبَطَلَ اعْتِرَاضُ مَنِ اعْتَرَضَ ) المعترض هو الشيخ أبو مدين في «شرح السلم»، فإنَّه قال: في الكلام تناقض، وبيدي نحو من عشرين مؤلفاً مِنَ الفنّ، وما منها إلا وقع له هذا التناقض.
His saying: 'And you have known the difference between them in concept and referent.' As for the difference in concept: because the proximate genus according to the first is the complete commonality between the quiddity and every quiddity that shares with it in it, and the low genus is that which has no genus under it and above it a genus. And as for referent: the growing body, for it according to the first division is a proximate genus relative to plant, because it is the complete commonality between it and everything that shares with it in it, unlike the second, so it is a middle genus, because above it is a genus which is absolute body, and under it a genus which is animal.
Note:
Just as the genus has four ranks, so also the relative species has four ranks:
1. The low species is that which has no species under it, and it is called 'species of species' because it is one of the relative species above it, like 'human'.
2. The high species is that which has no relative species above it, like 'body', for above it is only the high genus, which is substance.
3. The intermediate species is that which has a species above it and a species under it, like 'animal': above it is body, and under it is human.
4. The isolated species is that which has no species above it and no species under it, and its example is also impossible, except that it was exemplified by the intellect according to the philosophers, on the saying of whoever among them said: 'It is a species, and it falls under substance' as passed, and its having no species above it does not contradict that the genus is above it. So the objection of whoever objected to the two examples with it is invalid, and he exaggerated in that that making it from the divisions of the relative necessitates its composition, because it falls under a genus necessarily, while the isolated is not composed.
His saying: 'the relative species'. Some said: the correct is to drop this description, because the four ranks are only for absolute species; for the isolated species is not relative, and they made it from the relative. And the commentator followed in it al-Hilali who followed al-Sanusi who followed al-Khunaji, and Ibn Marzuq objected to this expression with what we mentioned.
And they only restricted 'species' with 'relative' because the true species cannot be ordered; because the true species cannot have another true species above it, otherwise the true species would be a genus, unlike relative species, for it is permissible that a relative species have another relative species above it, since there is no prevention.
His saying: 'and it falls under substance' i.e., so substance becomes a genus for it; it is said about it and about other things in answer to 'what is it?', and the ten intellects become individuals of it, not species, until another species is realized under it.
His saying: 'so the objection of whoever objected is invalid.' The objector is Shaykh Abu Madin in 'Sharh al-Sullam', for he said: there is a contradiction in the statement, and in my hand are about twenty works of the art, and not one of them except this contradiction occurs in it.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and dialectical discussion of the four ranks of relative species (al-naw' al-iḍāfī). It begins by continuing a commentary on a previous matn line, explaining the difference between proximate and low genus in concept and referent. Then it presents a note (tanbīh) that just as genus has four ranks (high, low, intermediate, and isolated), so species also has four. The low species (al-sāfil) is the most specific, with no species under it, like 'human'. The high species (al-ʿālī) has no relative species above it, like 'body', above which is only genus. The intermediate species (al-mutawassiṭ) has both a species above and below, like 'animal'. The isolated species (al-munfarid) has no species above or below; its example is difficult, but the philosophers cite 'intellect' which they consider a species falling under substance. The author defends this by noting that having no species above does not preclude having a genus above. Then he addresses an objection by Ibn Marzūq that calling this isolated species 'relative' is wrong because it is not relative, and explains why the term 'relative' is used: to distinguish from true species which cannot be ordered hierarchically. Finally, he identifies the objector as Shaykh Abu Madin and refutes his claim of contradiction.

Key Terms
النوع الإضافي
النوع السافل
النوع العالي
النوع المتوسط
النوع المنفرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the example given for the high species (al-naw' al-ʿālī)?
A) Human
B) Body
C) Intellect
D) Animal

Key Takeaway
The four ranks of relative species depend solely on the presence or absence of species above and below, not on genera.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Given the hierarchy: substance > body > animal > human, identify which rank each is (high species, intermediate, low).
?

Refuting an Objection on the Isolated Species
Refuting the objection that the isolated species cannot be relative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct and evaluate the objection that the isolated species cannot be a relative species, and explain the refutation.

Core Idea
The objector claimed a contradiction; the refutation shows that having no species above does not prevent having a genus above, so the species remains relative.

Some logicians, including Shaykh Abu Madin, objected that calling the isolated species (like intellect) a 'relative species' is contradictory because it has no species above or below, making it seem non-relative. The commentator refutes this by distinguishing between species and genus, and explains why the term 'relative' is still applicable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objector and their claim
Shaykh Abu Madin in his commentary on al-Sullam claimed that there is a contradiction in making the isolated species part of the relative species, because it would entail composition while the isolated is not composed.
The objector is identified at the end of the passage.
2
Extract the objection's logical basis
The objector thought that since the isolated species falls under a genus, it must have a composite nature, but the isolated species is supposed to be simple.
3
Summarize the refutation
The commentator argues that having no species above does not negate having a genus above. The isolated species can still be under a genus and be a species, so it is relative.
4
Explain why the term 'relative' is used
True species cannot be ordered hierarchically; relative species can. Even the isolated species has a genus above, so it is part of the hierarchy.
5
Assess the validity of the refutation
The refutation is sound because it uses the established definition of relative species, which allows a genus above.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَقَدْ عَلِمْتَ المُغَايَرَةَ بَيْنَهُمَا مَفْهُوماً وَمَصْدُوقاً أمَّا المغايرة في المفهوم : فلأنَّ الجنس القريب على الأوّل هو تمام المشترك بين الماهية وبين كلّ ماهية تشاركها فيه، والسافل هو الذي لا جنس تحته وفوقه جنس وأمَّا مصدوقاً : فالجسمُ النَّامي فإنَّه على التقسيم الأوّل جنس قريب بالنسبة إلى النبات; لأنَّه تمام المشترك بينه وبين كلّ ما يشاركه فيه بخلافه على الثَّاني، فهو جنس وسط; لأنَّ فوقه جنس وهو الجسم المطلق، وتحته جنس وهو الحيوان.

١ - فَالنَّوْعُ السَّافِلُ هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا نَوْعَ تَحْتَهُ، وَيُسَمَّى: «نَوْعَ الأَنْوَاعِ»; لِأَنَّهُ نَوْعٌ مِنَ الأَنْوَاعِ الإِضَافِيَّةِ الَّتِي فَوْقَهُ كَـ: «الإِنْسَانِ».

٤ - وَالنَّوْعُ المُنْفَرِدُ هُوَ: الَّذِي لَا نَوْعَ فَوْقَهُ، وَلَا نَوْعَ تَحْتَهُ، وَمِثَالُهُ أَيْضاً مُتَعَذِّرٌ; إِلَّا أَنَّهُ مُثْلَ لَهُ بِالعَقْلِ عِنْدَ الفَلَاسِفَةِ، عَلَى قَوْلِ مَنْ قَالَ مِنْهُمْ : «إِنَّهُ نَوْعٌ، وَإِنَّهُ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ الجَوْهَرِ» كَمَا مَرَّ ، وَكَوْنُهُ لَا نَوْعَ فَوْقَهُ لَا يُنَافِي أَنَّ الجِنْسَ فَوْقَهُ ، فَبَطَلَ اعْتِرَاضُ مَنِ اعْتَرَضَ عَلَى المُمَثْلَيْنِ بِهِ، وَهَوَّلَ فِي ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ جَعْلَهُ مِنْ أَقْسَامِ الإِضَافِي يَسْتَلْزِمُ تَرْكِيبَهُ; لِانْدِارَجِهِ تَحْتَ جِنْسِ حَتْماً، مَعَ أَنَّ المُنْفَرِدَ غَيْرُ مُرَكَّبٍ .
قوله : (النَّوْعُ الإِضَافِيُّ) قال بعضهم : الصَّوابُ إسقاط هذا الوصف ; لأنَّ الأربع مراتب إنَّما هي لمطلق النوع; إذ النوع المنفرد ليس بإضافي، وهم جعلوه مِنَ الإضافي، وقد تبع الشارح فيه الهلالي التابع للسَّنوسي التّابع للخونجي، وقد اعترض هذه العبارة ابن مرزوق بما ذكرنا .
وإنما قيَّدوا النوع بـ «الإضافي» ; لأنَّ الأنواع الحقيقيَّة يستحيل أن تترتب; لأنَّ النَّوع الحقيقيَّ لا يكون نوع آخر فوقه حقيقي، وإلا لكان النّوع الحقيقي جنساً بخلاف الأنواع الإضافية، فيجوز أن يكون نوعٌ إضافي فوقه نوع آخر إضافي; إذ لا منع .
قوله : (وَإِنَّهُ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ الجَوْهَرِ ) أي : فيكون الجوهر جنساً له; يقال عليه وعلى غيره في جواب «ما هو؟»، وتكون العقول العشرة أفراداً له لا أنواعاً حتّى يتحقق تحته نوع آخر .
قوله : (فَبَطَلَ اعْتِرَاضُ مَنِ اعْتَرَضَ ) المعترض هو الشيخ أبو مدين في «شرح السلم»، فإنَّه قال: في الكلام تناقض، وبيدي نحو من عشرين مؤلفاً مِنَ الفنّ، وما منها إلا وقع له هذا التناقض.
His saying: 'And you have known the difference between them in concept and referent.' As for the difference in concept: because the proximate genus according to the first is the complete commonality between the quiddity and every quiddity that shares with it in it, and the low genus is that which has no genus under it and above it a genus. And as for referent: the growing body, for it according to the first division is a proximate genus relative to plant, because it is the complete commonality between it and everything that shares with it in it, unlike the second, so it is a middle genus, because above it is a genus which is absolute body, and under it a genus which is animal.
Note:
Just as the genus has four ranks, so also the relative species has four ranks:
1. The low species is that which has no species under it, and it is called 'species of species' because it is one of the relative species above it, like 'human'.
2. The high species is that which has no relative species above it, like 'body', for above it is only the high genus, which is substance.
3. The intermediate species is that which has a species above it and a species under it, like 'animal': above it is body, and under it is human.
4. The isolated species is that which has no species above it and no species under it, and its example is also impossible, except that it was exemplified by the intellect according to the philosophers, on the saying of whoever among them said: 'It is a species, and it falls under substance' as passed, and its having no species above it does not contradict that the genus is above it. So the objection of whoever objected to the two examples with it is invalid, and he exaggerated in that that making it from the divisions of the relative necessitates its composition, because it falls under a genus necessarily, while the isolated is not composed.
His saying: 'the relative species'. Some said: the correct is to drop this description, because the four ranks are only for absolute species; for the isolated species is not relative, and they made it from the relative. And the commentator followed in it al-Hilali who followed al-Sanusi who followed al-Khunaji, and Ibn Marzuq objected to this expression with what we mentioned.
And they only restricted 'species' with 'relative' because the true species cannot be ordered; because the true species cannot have another true species above it, otherwise the true species would be a genus, unlike relative species, for it is permissible that a relative species have another relative species above it, since there is no prevention.
His saying: 'and it falls under substance' i.e., so substance becomes a genus for it; it is said about it and about other things in answer to 'what is it?', and the ten intellects become individuals of it, not species, until another species is realized under it.
His saying: 'so the objection of whoever objected is invalid.' The objector is Shaykh Abu Madin in 'Sharh al-Sullam', for he said: there is a contradiction in the statement, and in my hand are about twenty works of the art, and not one of them except this contradiction occurs in it.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and dialectical discussion of the four ranks of relative species (al-naw' al-iḍāfī). It begins by continuing a commentary on a previous matn line, explaining the difference between proximate and low genus in concept and referent. Then it presents a note (tanbīh) that just as genus has four ranks (high, low, intermediate, and isolated), so species also has four. The low species (al-sāfil) is the most specific, with no species under it, like 'human'. The high species (al-ʿālī) has no relative species above it, like 'body', above which is only genus. The intermediate species (al-mutawassiṭ) has both a species above and below, like 'animal'. The isolated species (al-munfarid) has no species above or below; its example is difficult, but the philosophers cite 'intellect' which they consider a species falling under substance. The author defends this by noting that having no species above does not preclude having a genus above. Then he addresses an objection by Ibn Marzūq that calling this isolated species 'relative' is wrong because it is not relative, and explains why the term 'relative' is used: to distinguish from true species which cannot be ordered hierarchically. Finally, he identifies the objector as Shaykh Abu Madin and refutes his claim of contradiction.

النوع المنفرد
النوع الإضافي
اعتراض
الجواب

Key Takeaway
The isolated species is still a relative species because it has a genus above, even if it lacks species above or below.

The Four Ranks of the Relative Type
Author defines the four ranks of the relative type with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify each of the four ranks of the relative type and provide an Islamic science example for each.

Core Idea
The relative type has four ranks, mirroring the genus; mastering them sharpens your logical toolkit for defining terms in Islamic sciences.

In logic, both genus and type are ordered hierarchically. The relative type (al-naw' al-idafi) has four ranks: lowest, highest, middle, and unique. This lesson introduces each rank with concrete examples from Kalam and falsafa, such as human, animal, body, substance, and intellect. Understanding these ranks is crucial for precise definition (hadd) in usul al-fiqh and theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rank by its relational position
Determine whether the type has a type above it, below it, both, or neither. This defines the rank.
The relative type is defined by its relation to other types, not by its own essence.
2
Note the examples for each rank
The passage provides: human (lowest), body (highest), animal (middle), intellect (unique). Understand why each fits its rank.
These examples are taken from Kalam and falsafa, not from everyday language.
3
Understand why the lowest is called 'naw' al-anwa''
The lowest type is a type among the types above it. 'Human' is a type under 'animal', which is under 'body', etc.
This helps in constructing hierarchies in definitions.
4
Distinguish highest from unique type
The highest type has no relative type above it, but has a genus above (e.g., body under substance). The unique type has no type above or below, but still has a genus.
Both have a genus, but the highest has types below it, while the unique does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه:
كَمَا أَنَّ الجِنْسَ لَهُ مَرَاتِبٌ أَرْبَعٌ ، كَذَلِكَ النَّوْعُ الإِضَافِيُّ لَهُ مَرَاتِبُ أَرْبَعُ ١ - فَالنَّوْعُ السَّافِلُ هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا نَوْعَ تَحْتَهُ، وَيُسَمَّى: «نَوْعَ الأَنْوَاعِ»؛ لِأَنَّهُ نَوْعٌ مِنَ الأَنْوَاعِ الإِضَافِيَّةِ الَّتِي فَوْقَهُ كَـ: «الإِنْسَانِ».
٢ - وَالنَّوْعُ العَالِي هُوَ : الَّذِي لَا نَوْعٌ إِضَافِيٌّ فَوْقَهُ كَ: «الجِسْمِ»، فَإِنَّهُ لَيْسَ فَوْقَهُ إِلَّا الجِنْسَ العَالِي ، وَهُوَ الجَوْهَرُ .
٣ - وَالنَّوْعُ المُتَوَسِّطُ هُوَ الَّذِي فَوْقَهُ نَوْعٌ وَتَحْتَهُ نَوْعٌ كَـ: «الحَيَوَانِ» فَوْقَهُ الجِسْمُ، وَتَحْتَهُ الإِنْسَانُ.
٤ - وَالنَّوْعُ المُنْفَرِدُ هُوَ: الَّذِي لَا نَوْعَ فَوْقَهُ، وَلَا نَوْعَ تَحْتَهُ، وَمِثَالُهُ أَيْضاً مُتَعَذِّرٌ؛ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ مُثْلَ لَهُ بِالعَقْلِ عِنْدَ الفَلَاسِفَةِ، عَلَى قَوْلِ مَنْ قَالَ مِنْهُمْ : «إِنَّهُ نَوْعٌ، وَإِنَّهُ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ الجَوْهَرِ»، كَمَا مَرَّ ، وَكَوْنُهُ لَا نَوْعَ فَوْقَهُ لَا يُنَافِي أَنَّ الجِنْسَ فَوْقَهُ ، فَبَطَلَ اعْتِرَاضُ مَنِ اعْتَرَضَ عَلَى المُمَثَّلِ بِهِ، وَهَوَّلَ فِي ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ جَعْلَهُ مِنْ أَقْسَامِ الإِضَافِي يَسْتَلْزِمُ تَرْكِيبَهُ؛ لِانْدِرَاجِهِ تَحْتَ جِنْسٍ حَتْماً، مَعَ أَنَّ المُنْفَرِدَ غَيْرُ مُرَكَّبٍ .
قوله : (النَّوْعُ الإِضَافِيُّ) قال بعضهم : الصَّوَابُ إسقاط هذا الوصف ؛ لأنَّ الأربع مراتب إنَّما هي لمطلق النوع؛ إذ النوع المنفرد ليس بإضافي، وهم جعلوه مِنَ الإضافي، وقد تبع الشارح فيه الهلالي التابع للسَّنوسي التّابع للخونجي، وقد اعترض هذه العبارة ابن مرزوق بما ذكرنا .
وإنما قيَّدوا النوع بـ «الإضافي» ؛ لأنَّ الأنواع الحقيقيَّة يستحيل أن تترتب؛ لأنَّ النَّوع الحقيقيَّ لا يكون نوع آخر فوقه حقيقي، وإلا لكان النّوع الحقيقي جنساً بخلاف الأنواع الإضافية، فيجوز أن يكون نوعٌ إضافي فوقه نوع آخر إضافي؛ إذ لا منع .
قوله : (وَإِنَّهُ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ الجَوْهَرِ ) أي : فيكون الجوهر جنساً له؛ يقال عليه وعلى غيره في جواب «ما هو؟»، وتكون العقول العشرة أفراداً له لا أنواعاً حتّى يتحقق تحته نوع آخر .
قوله : (فَبَطَلَ اعْتِرَاضُ مَنِ اعْتَرَضَ ) المعترض هو الشيخ أبو مدين في «شرح السلم»، فإنَّه قال: في الكلام تناقض، وبيدي نحو من عشرين مؤلفاً مِنَ الفنّ، وما منها إلا وقع له هذا التناقض.
وجوابه ما أشار له الشَّارح تبعاً للهلالي رحمه الله تعالى وحاصله: ليس المراد بـ «المنفرد» في هذا التقسيم : البسيط الذي لا تركيب فيه حتّى يقتضي ذلك عدم اندراجه تحت جنس، فلا يكون نوعاً إضافيًا، بل المراد ما لا نوع تحته ولا نوع فوقه إضافي، وإنما فوقه الجنس الذي أوجب كونه نوعاً إضافيًا، وحينئذ فلا إشكال في صحة التمثيل به لكن الاعتراض على المثال أمره خفيف ؛ لأنَّه لا يلزم من فساد المثال فساد الممثل له ، ولذلك شاع على الألسنة : الاعتراض على المثال ليس من دأب الرجال.
Note: Just as the genus has four ranks, likewise the relative type has four ranks. 1) The lowest type is that which has no type below it, and it is called 'the type of types' because it is a type among the relative types above it, like 'human'. 2) The highest type is that which has no relative type above it, like 'body', for there is nothing above it except the highest genus, which is substance. 3) The middle type is that which has a type above it and a type below it, like 'animal': above it is 'body', and below it is 'human'. 4) The unique type is that which has no type above it and no type below it; its example is also difficult, except that it is exemplified by the intellect according to the philosophers, based on the statement of those among them who said: 'It is a type, and it is subsumed under substance,' as previously mentioned. And the fact that it has no type above it does not contradict that the genus is above it. So the objection of one who objected to what is exemplified by it is invalidated, and he exaggerated in that by saying that making it one of the divisions of the relative type necessitates its composition, because it is necessarily subsumed under a genus, while the unique type is not composite. His statement: (The relative type) Some said: The correct thing is to drop this description, because the four ranks are for the absolute type; for the unique type is not relative, yet they made it among the relative. The commentator followed in this al-Hilali, who followed al-Sanusi, who followed al-Khwanji, and Ibn Marzuq objected to this statement with what we mentioned. They only restricted the type with 'relative' because the real types cannot be arranged, because a real type cannot have another real type above it, otherwise the real type would be a genus, unlike the relative types, for it is permissible that a relative type has another relative type above it, as there is no prohibition. His statement: (And that it is subsumed under substance) meaning that substance is a genus for it; it is said of it and of others in answer to 'What is it?', and the ten intellects are individuals of it, not types, so that there is no other type under it. His statement: (So the objection of one who objected is invalidated) The objector is Shaykh Abu Madin in his commentary on al-Sullam, for he said: There is a contradiction in the statement, and I have about twenty works from the craft, and there is none of them except that this contradiction occurs. And its answer is what the commentator indicated following al-Hilali, may Allah have mercy on him, and its summary: What is meant by 'the unique' in this division is not the simple that has no composition such that it necessitates not being subsumed under a genus, so it would not be a relative type; rather, what is meant is that which has no type below it and no relative type above it, and above it is only the genus that necessitated it being a relative type. Then there is no problem in the validity of exemplifying with it. But the objection to the example is a light matter, because the corruption of the example does not necessitate the corruption of what is exemplified by it. Therefore it is common on tongues: Objecting to the example is not the practice of men.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage defines the four ranks of the relative type (al-naw' al-idafi) and resolves an objection concerning the example of the intellect. The author begins by drawing an analogy with the four ranks of the genus, then enumerates each rank. 

1) The lowest type (al-naw' al-safil) has no type below it; it is called 'naw' al-anwa'' (type of types) because it is a type among the relative types above it, e.g., 'human'. 
2) The highest type (al-naw' al-'ali) has no relative type above it, e.g., 'body', above which is only the highest genus (substance). 
3) The middle type (al-naw' al-mutawassit) has a type both above and below, e.g., 'animal' (above: body; below: human). 
4) The unique type (al-naw' al-munfarid) has no type above or below. An example is difficult, but philosophers suggest 'intellect' ('aql'), considering it a type under the genus of substance. 

The author then addresses an objection: some argue that making the intellect a relative type implies it is composite, whereas the unique type is simple. The response clarifies that 'unique' here refers to having no type above or below in the relative sense, not to absolute simplicity; it can still have a genus, making it a relative type. The author further notes a scholarly chain for this classification (al-Hilali → al-Sanusi → al-Khwanji) and an objection by Ibn Marzuq. The passage concludes with the principle that a flawed example does not invalidate the classification, and objecting to examples is not the practice of serious scholars. All examples used are from the Islamic sciences: human, animal, body, substance, and intellect (as used by philosophers).

النوع السافل
النوع العالي

النوع المنفرد

The four ranks of the relative type (lowest, highest, middle, unique) organise types based on their relations to other types, enabling precise definition and classification in Islamic logic.

Resolving the Objection about the Intellect as Unique Type
Author resolves an objection regarding the intellect as an example of the unique type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the objection against the intellect as an example of the unique type and explain the commentator’s resolution using the distinction between relative type and simplicity.

Core Idea
The objection that the unique type cannot be composite is resolved by distinguishing between having a genus (which makes it relative) and having a type above it.

In the previous lesson, you learned that philosophers exemplify the unique type by the intellect. However, some scholars objected that this is contradictory because the intellect is simple yet subsumed under a genus. This lesson presents the objection and the commentator’s response, showing how careful logical distinctions save the classification. The discussion also involves a chain of authorities (Hilali, Sanusi, Khwanji) and the principle that a flawed example does not invalidate a classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objector and his claim
Shaykh Abu Madin claimed a contradiction: the intellect is a relative type (implying composition) but the unique type is supposed to be simple.
He refers to 'about twenty works' where this contradiction appears.
2
Understand the basis of the objection
The objector assumes 'unique' means absolutely simple, with no composition at all. Being under a genus implies composition (genus + differentia).
This is a misinterpretation of the term 'munfarid'.
3
Follow the commentator's response
The commentator explains that 'unique' in this classification means having no relative type above or below, not having no genus. The intellect has a genus (substance) but no type above or below.
Thus, it is still a relative type without contradiction.
4
Note the scholarly chain
The author follows al-Hilali, who followed al-Sanusi, who followed al-Khwanji. Ibn Marzuq also objected to calling the unique type 'relative'.
This shows the development of the concept.
5
Apply the principle of example vs. classification
Even if the example (intellect) were flawed, the classification itself remains valid. Objecting to an example is not a serious scholarly practice.
The passage ends with a common saying: 'Objecting to the example is not the practice of men.'
