قوله : (النَّوْعُ الإِضَافِيُّ) قال بعضهم : الصَّوَابُ إسقاط هذا الوصف ؛ لأنَّ الأربع مراتب إنَّما هي لمطلق النوع؛ إذ النوع المنفرد ليس بإضافي، وهم جعلوه مِنَ الإضافي، وقد تبع الشارح فيه الهلالي التابع للسَّنوسي التّابع للخونجي، وقد اعترض هذه العبارة ابن مرزوق بما ذكرنا .
وإنما قيَّدوا النوع بـ «الإضافي» ؛ لأنَّ الأنواع الحقيقيَّة يستحيل أن تترتب؛ لأنَّ النَّوع الحقيقيَّ لا يكون نوع آخر فوقه حقيقي، وإلا لكان النّوع الحقيقي جنساً بخلاف الأنواع الإضافية، فيجوز أن يكون نوعٌ إضافي فوقه نوع آخر إضافي؛ إذ لا منع .
قوله : (وَإِنَّهُ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ الجَوْهَرِ ) أي : فيكون الجوهر جنساً له؛ يقال عليه وعلى غيره في جواب «ما هو؟»، وتكون العقول العشرة أفراداً له لا أنواعاً حتّى يتحقق تحته نوع آخر .
قوله : (فَبَطَلَ اعْتِرَاضُ مَنِ اعْتَرَضَ ) المعترض هو الشيخ أبو مدين في «شرح السلم»، فإنَّه قال: في الكلام تناقض، وبيدي نحو من عشرين مؤلفاً مِنَ الفنّ، وما منها إلا وقع له هذا التناقض.
وجوابه ما أشار له الشَّارح تبعاً للهلالي رحمه الله تعالى وحاصله: ليس المراد بـ «المنفرد» في هذا التقسيم : البسيط الذي لا تركيب فيه حتّى يقتضي ذلك عدم اندراجه تحت جنس، فلا يكون نوعاً إضافيًا، بل المراد ما لا نوع تحته ولا نوع فوقه إضافي، وإنما فوقه الجنس الذي أوجب كونه نوعاً إضافيًا، وحينئذ فلا إشكال في صحة التمثيل به لكن الاعتراض على المثال أمره خفيف ؛ لأنَّه لا يلزم من فساد المثال فساد الممثل له ، ولذلك شاع على الألسنة : الاعتراض على المثال ليس من دأب الرجال.
Note: Just as the genus has four ranks, likewise the relative type has four ranks. 1) The lowest type is that which has no type below it, and it is called 'the type of types' because it is a type among the relative types above it, like 'human'. 2) The highest type is that which has no relative type above it, like 'body', for there is nothing above it except the highest genus, which is substance. 3) The middle type is that which has a type above it and a type below it, like 'animal': above it is 'body', and below it is 'human'. 4) The unique type is that which has no type above it and no type below it; its example is also difficult, except that it is exemplified by the intellect according to the philosophers, based on the statement of those among them who said: 'It is a type, and it is subsumed under substance,' as previously mentioned. And the fact that it has no type above it does not contradict that the genus is above it. So the objection of one who objected to what is exemplified by it is invalidated, and he exaggerated in that by saying that making it one of the divisions of the relative type necessitates its composition, because it is necessarily subsumed under a genus, while the unique type is not composite. His statement: (The relative type) Some said: The correct thing is to drop this description, because the four ranks are for the absolute type; for the unique type is not relative, yet they made it among the relative. The commentator followed in this al-Hilali, who followed al-Sanusi, who followed al-Khwanji, and Ibn Marzuq objected to this statement with what we mentioned. They only restricted the type with 'relative' because the real types cannot be arranged, because a real type cannot have another real type above it, otherwise the real type would be a genus, unlike the relative types, for it is permissible that a relative type has another relative type above it, as there is no prohibition. His statement: (And that it is subsumed under substance) meaning that substance is a genus for it; it is said of it and of others in answer to 'What is it?', and the ten intellects are individuals of it, not types, so that there is no other type under it. His statement: (So the objection of one who objected is invalidated) The objector is Shaykh Abu Madin in his commentary on al-Sullam, for he said: There is a contradiction in the statement, and I have about twenty works from the craft, and there is none of them except that this contradiction occurs. And its answer is what the commentator indicated following al-Hilali, may Allah have mercy on him, and its summary: What is meant by 'the unique' in this division is not the simple that has no composition such that it necessitates not being subsumed under a genus, so it would not be a relative type; rather, what is meant is that which has no type below it and no relative type above it, and above it is only the genus that necessitated it being a relative type. Then there is no problem in the validity of exemplifying with it. But the objection to the example is a light matter, because the corruption of the example does not necessitate the corruption of what is exemplified by it. Therefore it is common on tongues: Objecting to the example is not the practice of men.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage defines the four ranks of the relative type (al-naw' al-idafi) and resolves an objection concerning the example of the intellect. The author begins by drawing an analogy with the four ranks of the genus, then enumerates each rank. 

1) The lowest type (al-naw' al-safil) has no type below it; it is called 'naw' al-anwa'' (type of types) because it is a type among the relative types above it, e.g., 'human'. 
2) The highest type (al-naw' al-'ali) has no relative type above it, e.g., 'body', above which is only the highest genus (substance). 
3) The middle type (al-naw' al-mutawassit) has a type both above and below, e.g., 'animal' (above: body; below: human). 
4) The unique type (al-naw' al-munfarid) has no type above or below. An example is difficult, but philosophers suggest 'intellect' ('aql'), considering it a type under the genus of substance. 

The author then addresses an objection: some argue that making the intellect a relative type implies it is composite, whereas the unique type is simple. The response clarifies that 'unique' here refers to having no type above or below in the relative sense, not to absolute simplicity; it can still have a genus, making it a relative type. The author further notes a scholarly chain for this classification (al-Hilali → al-Sanusi → al-Khwanji) and an objection by Ibn Marzuq. The passage concludes with the principle that a flawed example does not invalidate the classification, and objecting to examples is not the practice of serious scholars. All examples used are from the Islamic sciences: human, animal, body, substance, and intellect (as used by philosophers).

Key Terms
النوع المنفرد
النوع الإضافي
النوع الحقيقي
الجنس
العقل

A) Al-Sanusi
B) Shaykh Abu Madin
C) Ibn Marzuq
D) Al-Khwanji

Key Takeaway
The objection that the intellect cannot be an example of the unique type is resolved by distinguishing between having a genus (which allows it to be a relative type) and having a type above it (which it lacks).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
In a discussion about the classification of 'jinn' (spirits), if someone objects that they cannot be a unique type because they have a genus (e.g., 'created invisible being'), explain whether this objection is valid using the reasoning from this lesson.

The Five Universals

The Five Relations of Words and the Univocal
Author defines the five relations and explains the derivation, then defines univocal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any Arabic word into one of the five relations and distinguish between univocal and analogical using the criteria of equality vs. gradation.

Core Idea
A single word for a single meaning splits into equal (univocal) or graded (analogical).

In Islamic logic (Mantiq), understanding how words relate to meanings is crucial for precise definition and sound argument. This passage from al-Bajuri’s commentary lays out the five possible relations, focusing especially on the univocal—where all individuals share the meaning equally. You will learn to navigate this classification, which directly feeds into later discussions of universals and definitions.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the logical grid
The author derives the five relations from two binary distinctions: word is one or multiple, meaning is one or multiple. This gives four basic combinations. The first combination (one word, one meaning) is then split into univocal (equal) and analogical (graded), making five total.
Memorize the grid: word×meaning combos → 2+2+1=5.
2
Identify the five terms
The passage lists: تواطؤ (univocal), تشاكك (analogical), تخالف (diverse), اشتراك (shared), ترادف (synonymous). Practice naming them in Arabic and English.
The Arabic terms are precise; note that تشاكك is analogical (not to be confused with doubt).
3
Define univocal (المتواطئ)
The univocal is a universal whose external individuals are equal in its meaning, e.g., 'human' – all humans are equally human. No individual is more deserving of the meaning.
This is a hadd (real definition) with genus (universal) and differentia (equality).
4
Contrast with analogical (المشكك)
Analogical terms apply to individuals in varying degrees or by priority, e.g., 'wujūd' (existence) is more intense in God than creatures. The marginal note gives example 'wajada' (found) with nuances.
In Islamic theology, 'wujūd' is a classic analogical term.
5
Test the definition with the objection
The passage ends with an objection: some humans (e.g., prophets) seem more deserving of 'humanity' due to their rational perfection. Consider whether this challenges the univocal definition or misconceives it.
The logician’s response is that humanity is about species essence, not perfection; the objection confuses attribute with essence.

فَصْلٌ فِي بَيَانِ نِسْبَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي) (۳۳) وَنِسْبَةُ الأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي خَمْسَةُ أَقْسَامٍ بِلَا نُقْصَانِ: (٣٤) تَوَاطُؤٌ، تَشَاكُكُ، تَخَالُفٌ، وَالاشْتِراكُ، عَكْسُهُ التَّرَادُفُ قَسَمَ اللَّفْظَ - أي : الكُلّي - إِلَى خَمْسَةِ أَقْسَامِ، وَوَجْهُ الحَصْرِ فِيهَا أَنْ تَقُولَ : اللَّفْظُ إِمَّا وَاحِدٌ أَوْ مُتَعَدِّدٌ، وَالمَعْنَى فِي كُلِّ مِنْهُمَا: إِمَّا وَاحِدٌ أَوْ مُتَعَدِّدٌ؛ فَهَذِهِ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَامٍ، وَالقِسْمُ الأَوَّلُ مِنْهَا وَهُوَ لَفْظُ وَاحِدٌ لِمَعْنَى وَاحِدٍ قِسْمَانِ : مُتَوَاطِئُ وَمُشَكَّكٌ، وَبِذَلِكَ كَانَتْ خَمْسَةَ أَقْسَامٍ. فَالمُتَوَاطِيُّ هُوَ : الكُلِّيُّ الَّذِي تَسَاوَتْ فِي مَعْنَاهُ أَفْرَادُهُ الخَارِجِيَّةُ كَـ: «الإِنْسَانِ»، فَإِنَّ أَفْرَادَهُ كَـ: زَيْدٍ وَعَمْرِو مُتَسَاوِيَةٌ فِي الإِنْسَانِيَّةِ ، وَلَيْسَ بَعْضُهَا أَوْلَى مِنْ بَعْضٍ بِهَا . قصارة. قول النَّاظم : (وَنِسْبَةُ الأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي) ظاهر إطلاقه يقتضي أنَّ هذه النسب تأتي في الفعل، وهو كذلك ؛ فالمتواطئ كـ «ذهب»، والمشكك كـ «وجد»، والمتباين كـ: «قام، وقعد»، والمترادف كـ «جلس، وقعد»، والمشترك كـ «عسعس» لـ: «أقبل وأدبر». ويقتضي أنَّ هذه النسب تكون في المفرد وفي المركب مع أنه لم يأت في المركب إلَّا البعض، وهو الاشتراك، ومثله العقباني بـ : أراق دمي ؛ لأنه يحتمل الإخبار برؤية القدم، أو بإراقة الدم، أَرَاقَ دَمِـ ومنه قول بعضهم : إِلَى حَتْفِي مَشَى قَدَمِي أَرَى قَدَمِ واعترض بأنَّ هذا في اللفظ لا في الرَّقم، فصوابُ التَّمثيل : «دعاني»، فإنَّه يكون أمراً للاثنين، وإخباراً عن مفرد غائب، وقد اجتمعا في قوله : دَعَانِي مَنْ مَلَامِكُمَا سَفَاهَا فَدَاعِي الشَّوْقِ قَبْلُكُمَا دَعَانِي قوله : (وَلَيْسَ بَعْضُهَا أَوْلَى مِنْ بَعْضٍ فإن قلت : يَرِدُ عليه أنَّ كثيراً من أفراد الإنسان أولى بمعناه من بعض؛ لشدة فطنته، وحدة فؤاده، واشتماله على لطائف هي أليق بناطقيته، وأبعد عن جانب غيره من الحيوانات؛ كما قيل:
Chapter on explaining the relation of words to meanings. (33) The relation of words to meanings is five divisions without deficiency: (34) univocal, analogical, diverse, and shared, its opposite is synonymous. He divided the word—meaning the universal—into five divisions. The justification for confining them is that you say: The word is either one or multiple, and the meaning in each of them is either one or multiple; these are four divisions. The first division, which is one word for one meaning, is two divisions: univocal and analogical. Thus they became five divisions. The univocal is the universal whose external individuals are equal in its meaning, like 'human', for its individuals like Zayd and 'Amr are equal in humanity, and not some of them are more deserving of it than others. Marginal note: The author's saying: 'And the relation of words to meanings' — its apparent generality implies that these relations occur in verbs, and it is so. The univocal like 'dhahaba' (he went), the analogical like 'wajada' (he found), the diverse like 'qāma' (he stood) and 'qa'ada' (he sat), the synonymous like 'jalasa' (he sat) and 'qa'ada' (he sat), and the shared like 'ʿasʿasa' for 'he approached' and 'he withdrew'. It also implies that these relations occur in the single word and in the compound, although only some occur in the compound, namely shared. An example of the latter is 'arāqa damī' (he shed my blood?) because it can mean informing of seeing the foot or shedding blood. And from it is the saying of some: 'To my death walked my foot, I see my foot.' It was objected that this is in the utterance, not in the written form, so the correct example is 'daʿānī' (he called me) because it can be a command for two or a report about a third singular male. Both occur in his saying: 'He called me, one of your blame foolishly; so the caller of longing before you called me.' His saying: 'And not some of them are more deserving than others' — for if you say: it is objected against it that many individuals of human are more deserving of its meaning than others, due to their strong intelligence, sharpness of heart, and inclusion of subtleties more fitting to their rationality and more distant from the side of other animals; as it is said:
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of the five relations between words and their meanings, a foundational topic in Islamic logic. It begins by stating the five divisions: univocal (تواطؤ), analogical (تشاكك), diverse (تخالف), shared (اشتراك), and synonymous (ترادف). The author then explains how these five derive from four logical combinations: a word can be one or multiple, and the meaning can be one or multiple. The first combination (one word, one meaning) is further subdivided into univocal (where the meaning applies equally) and analogical (where it applies by priority). The univocal is defined as a universal whose external individuals share the meaning equally, exemplified by 'human' (إنسان) where all individuals are equally human. The marginal gloss then provides examples for each type using verbs and compounds, and discusses issues with some examples. It also raises an objection about the equality claim: some humans are more deserving of the meaning 'human' due to their superior rational faculties. The passage ends mid-objection.

المشكك
الاشتراك
الترادف

Key Takeaway
The five relations (univocal, analogical, diverse, shared, synonymous) cover all word-meaning mappings, with univocal being the baseline where meaning applies equally to all individuals.

The Four Types of Tabayun and the Four Relative Proportions
Classification of tabayun into four types and statement of the four relative proportions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any pair of terms into one of the four types of tabayun (difference) based on their concept and extension, and identify which of the four relative proportions holds between them.

Core Idea
Tabayun is not just total difference—it includes partial overlap in concept or extension.

In logic, we often need to compare terms to see if they are synonyms or different. But 'difference' (tabayun) has gradations. A pair of terms may differ in meaning completely, or they may share some extension while differing in concept, or they may overlap partially. This lesson teaches you the precise classification that logicians use to analyze such relationships, which is essential for clear reasoning in Islamic sciences like usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify if the difference is in both concept and extension
Check if the two terms apply to completely different sets of individuals and have different meanings. Example: 'man' and 'stone' – no overlap in extension, and concepts are different.
This is the first type: total tabayun.
2
If not total, check if they differ in concept only
If the two terms apply to the same or overlapping individuals but have different meanings, then difference is in concept only. Now check whether their extensions are equal or not.
3
If extensions are equal, it's second type
Example: 'laughing' and 'rational' – both apply to all humans, but meanings differ. This is tabayun in concept only with equal extension.
4
If extensions are not equal, determine one-way or two-way overlap
If one term's extension is a subset of the other's, it's 'umum wa khusus mutlaq' (absolute generality/specificity), e.g., 'animal' (more general) and 'man' (more specific). If each term applies to some individuals the other does not, it's 'umum wa khusus min wajh' (two-way partial overlap), e.g., 'man' and 'black'.
These are the third and fourth types.
5
Apply the four relative proportions
Any two concepts have one of four relationships: total exclusion (first type), identity in extension but difference in concept (second type), one-way generality (third type), or two-way partial overlap (fourth type). Practice by classifying pairs from fiqh or kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان نسبة الألفاظ للمعاني » : ۵۲۷ وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ التَّباينَ بِالمَعْنَى المَذْكُورِ - أَيْ : مُقَابِلِ التَّرَادُفِ - يَقَعُ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَقْسَام ; لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يَكُونُ كُلّيّا فِي المَفْهُومِ وَالمَصْدُوقِ بِأَنْ لَا يَصْدُقَ أَحَدُهُمَا عَلَى شَيْءٍ مِمَّا يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهِ الآخَرُ : الإِنْسَانِ، وَ: «الحَجَرِ»، وَمِنْهُ تَبَايِنُ المُشْتَقِّ وَالمُشْتَقِّ مِنْهُ كَـ: «العِلْمِ»، و: «العَالِمِ»، وَقَدْ يَكُونُ فِي المَفْهُومِ فَقَط ، وَذَلِكَ إِمَّا مَعَ تَسَاوِيهِمَا فِي المَصْدُوقِ گ: «الصَّاحِكِ»، وَ: «النَّاطِقِ، وَإِمَّا مَعَ عَدَمِ التَّسَاوِي بِأَنْ يَفْتَرِفًا فِي بَعْضِ أَفْرَادِ المَصْدُوقِ، وَالاِفْتِرَاقُ إِمَّا مِنْ جِهَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَهُوَ العُمُومُ وَالخُصُوصُ بِإِطْلَاقِ گ: «الحَيَوَانِ»، وَ: «الإِنْسَانِ»، فَالأَكْثَرُ أَفْرَاداً أَعَمُّ ، وَالأَقَلُّ أَخَصُّ ، وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ الصِّفَةُ وَالمَوْصُوفُ : السَّيْفِ ، وَ : «الصَّارِمِ، وَكَـ: «النَّاطِقِ، وَ: «الفَصِيحِ، وَإِمَّا مِنَ كَـ الجِهَتَيْنِ مَعاً وَهُوَ العُمُومُ وَالخُصُوصُ مِنْ وَجْهِ كَـ: الإِنْسَانِ، وَ: «الأَسْوَدِ»، وَكَـ: «الصَّارِمِ»، وَ: «المُهَنَّدِ ، وَهَذِهِ هِيَ النِّسَبُ الأَرْبَعُ الَّتِي لَا بُدَّ بَيْنَ كُلِّ مَعْقُولَيْنِ مِنْ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهَا (١) قصارة قوله : (گـ: «العِلْمِ، وَ العَالِمِ) فإنَّ معنى «العلم» كما قال القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني: «معرفة المعلوم، ومعنى العالم : الذَّات المتّصفة بالعِلم، ولا فرق بين أن يكون معنى المشتق منه قائماً بالمشتق كالمثال، أو موضوعاً لمحل عمل كالحديد للحداد، فإنَّ الحديد الذي هو مشتق منه موضوع للجسم الشَّديد الأسود، وهو محل عمل للحداد الذي هو المشتق؛ أي: يعمل منه الأشياء كالسيوف والدروع، وغير ذلك، فقولُ قدُّورة : موضوعاً لعمل على حذف مضاف؛ أي: محل عمل، أو يكون موجداً له؛ أي: يكون المشتقُ سبباً مجازيًا في وجود المشتق منه كالمال والمتموّل، فإنَّ الموجد للمال بسبب التجارة وغيرها هو المتموّل ; أي: صاحب المال . قوله : (وَهَذِهِ هِيَ النِّسَبُ الأَرْبَعُ ... إلخ) اعلم أنَّ هذه النِّسب إن اعتبرت بين المفردين كانت معتبرةً بينهما في الحمل; نحو: كلُّ إنسان ناطق، وبالعكس، وفي الوجود; أي: كلَّما الإنسان وجد الناطق، وإن اعتبرت بين القضيَّتين كانت معتبرةً في الوجود فقط دون الصدق; إذ لا يتصوَّر حمل القضايا على شيء. وجد وتتعرض الشارح لذكر هذه النسب; لأنَّ المحلَّ لائق بها فهي فائدة حسنة، وقد أشار لها صاحب القادرية» بقوله : (۱) في :(أ) مِنْهُمَا، بدلاً من مِنْهَا».
Chapter on explaining the relationship of words to meanings. Know that tabayun (difference) in the mentioned sense – i.e., the opposite of taraduf (synonymy) – occurs in four divisions. For it may be total in concept and extension, i.e., one does not apply to any of what the other applies to, like 'man' and 'stone'. Among this is the difference between the derived word and its source, like 'knowledge' and 'knower'. And it may be in concept only, either with equality in extension, like 'laughing' and 'rational', or without equality, i.e., they differ in some members of extension. The difference is either from one side, which is absolute generality and specificity, like 'animal' and 'man' – the larger in number of individuals is more general, the smaller more specific – and from that are the attribute and the described, like 'sword' and 'sharp', and like 'rational' and 'eloquent'. Or it may be from both sides together, which is generality and specificity from a perspective, like 'man' and 'black', and like 'sharp' and 'Indian [sword]'. These are the four relative proportions that must exist between any two intelligibles: one of them. [Commentary:] His saying: 'like knowledge and knower' – for the meaning of 'knowledge' as Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani said is 'cognition of the known', and the meaning of 'knower' is the essence characterized by knowledge. There is no difference between the meaning of the derived source being inherent in the derivative like the example, or being the subject of an operation like iron for the blacksmith, for iron which is the derived source is placed for the intense black body, and it is the locus of work for the blacksmith who is the derivative, i.e., he makes things from it like swords and armor and so forth. So the saying of Qaddura: 'subject to work' is with an omitted genitive, i.e., locus of work, or it is a cause of its existence, i.e., the derivative is a metaphorical cause of the existence of the source, like wealth and the wealthy, for the one who brings wealth into existence through trade etc. is the wealthy, i.e., the owner of wealth. His saying: 'These are the four relative proportions... etc.' Know that these proportions, if considered between two singular terms, are considered between them in predication, e.g., every man is rational, and the reverse, and in existence, i.e., whenever man exists, rational exists. If considered between two propositions, they are considered in existence only, not truth, since predication of propositions on something is not conceivable. The commentator mentions these proportions because the context is suitable for them, and it is a good benefit. The author of al-Qadiriyya alluded to them in his poem.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the types of 'tabayun' (difference) between words in terms of meaning, as opposed to synonymy. The author states that tabayun can be of four types. First, total difference in both concept and extension (e.g., 'man' and 'stone'), including the case of derived terms and their sources (e.g., 'knowledge' and 'knower'), where the concept differs but the extension may overlap. Second, difference in concept only, which can be (a) with equal extension (e.g., 'laughing' and 'rational', both applying to humans), or (b) without equality, which is further divided: (i) one-way generality/specificity (e.g., 'animal' and 'man') – also seen in attribute-description pairs like 'sword' and 'sharp' – and (ii) two-way partial overlap (generality and specificity from a perspective, e.g., 'man' and 'black'). The author then declares these to be the four relative proportions that necessarily hold between any two concepts. The commentary expands on the example of 'knowledge' and 'knower', explaining that the relationship between a derivative and its source can be one of inherence, of subject-locus, or of metaphorical causation. The comment concludes by noting that these proportions apply to singular terms in terms of predication and existence, but to propositions only in terms of existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following pairs exhibits 'umum wa khusus mutlaq' (one-way generality/specificity)?
A) 'Man' and 'stone'
B) 'Laughing' and 'rational'
C) 'Animal' and 'man'
D) 'Man' and 'black'

Key Takeaway
Any two concepts have one of four relationships: total exclusion, identical extension with different concept, one-way generality, or two-way partial overlap.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify the following pairs of terms into one of the four types of tabayun: (i) 'wudu' and 'tahara', (ii) 'salat' and 'du'a', (iii) 'iman' and 'islam', (iv) 'haram' and 'makruh'. For each, state the type and justify using concept and extension.
?
Take a real usul al-fiqh issue: the terms 'amm' (general) and 'khas' (specific). Which of the four relative proportions holds between 'amm' and 'khas'? Explain using examples from the Quran (e.g., 'al-nas' and 'al-mu'minun').
